RATING: 5.5
*Rating based on one 2 vs 2 team game.

+Easy-to-learn rules set.
+Lots of factions to choose from.

=Artwork and component quality pretty standard.
=More of a tactical than a deep strategy game.
=Dice rolling for attacks adds some randomness.

-Preset starting setup seems limiting.  I would have preferred some way for players to choose their own starting forces and deployment.
-Players draw cards at the start of their turn, meaning it's impossible to plan out your turn ahead of time, increasing the play time.
-Player elimination in the team game can leave someone sitting and watching for a significant portion of the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Avoided Summoner Wars for the first few years, rationalizing it with the few negative reviews out there.  Then, a few days ago, while checking in on the game I realized that it not only had established a very sizable fan base, but that it occupies a unique niche in most nearly collection.  

The rules are stoopid simple, the gameplay is obvious beyond belief, and yet the factions and their different cards are all so brilliantly constructed that this quick-playing game can easily hog all your table-time.   This is the genius of Summoner Wars -- it's not the rules, the art, it's the armies themselves, and the interplay between their match-ups.  

I realize this game isn't for everyone, but I can't think of any particular class of gamer that shouldn't check this out.  Open your mind, and give it a couple of plays, and I think you'll appreciate just how sublime this game's design really is.

Oh, and everyone hating on the artwork is entirely too judgemental.  Based on the Master Set alone, there's not a freakin' thing wrong with the art.  Sure, a few colors could've been different and stuff like that, but to say anything is like trying to send back a steak because your beer is too cold.  Shuddup and enjoy the bleepin' game!

The one criticism I have is that the game can feel very "claustrophobic" in the sense that movement is often severely constrained and you can often feel like you just don't have any good options to chose from.  Well, welcome to wargaming -- you did realize that Summoner Wars is a wargame underneath those deceptively simple rules, right?

RATING: 6
A great game that suffers from a few flaws.  Firstly it has a lot of downtime.  There's very little to do while your opponent is thinking and not much point planning since the board changes radically after each turn.  Few interrupt cards as well and you can't even look at your hand until the start of your turn, i.e. more downtime.  Another problem is that it's only two player so doesn't hit the table that much, and although the Master Set comes from a great board, I wouldn't say the game is great value for money.  Unless you're hungry for tactical card games with a fantasy theme I wouldn't recommend this, despite it being a pretty cool game.

UPDATE: I'd recommend Mage Wars over this game pretty much every time...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
I've updated the comments because it seems I'm the only person who thinks this game is fatally flawed. 

The luck in this game is crippling. It's not just the arbitrariness of the 3+ dice rolling, which IS awful if only because you just can't cater to those kind of odds.
 
It's more that the skill of the game is maneuvering to minimise the powerful effects of your opponents. The reality is that it just doesn't matter because the champions are so diverse that you never really know what you're up against.

The whole thing means you just play each turn as well as you can and hope for the best. When you throw in things like Magic Drain and killing your own guys to preserve magic, the whole game lacks any cohesion. Summoner Wars is Chess, Magic, Poker etc. for people who like all of those games but weren't good at any of them. It's a nice glossy product with this Master Set, but it just isn't strategically compelling to me. 

I know this game has thousands of fans, but I've never found anything they've said to overturn these sentiments. This is a game for breadth gamers who think they're depth gaming.

RATING: 8
Yet again, rival bands of fantasy folk do battle across featureless terrain.  No, the theme of Summoner Wars doesn't excite me.

Beyond the hackneyed theme there is a pretty neat little game.  The rules are simple enough to explain in a couple of minutes.  However, each turn presents tricky  decisions about what to summon, what to move and attack, how to protect your Summoner and how many events and warriors to convert into magic points.  On top of that, each of the six bands of fantasy folk included has it's own character, which alters all those tricky decisions. In my experience, games that don't go to the bitter end of depleted decks are few.  A few of those longer games have felt like an attritional trudge, but mostly I've been having fun exploring the different decks.

Production quality is good.  The artwork is unexciting, with a surfeit of murky greys and browns.  The rules are well written and seem complete.

RATING: 9
Egy kicsit sakkra emlékeztető játék, csak itt a táblán figurák helyett kártyák vannak, amikkel mozogni, támadni lehet, cél a főellenség megölése. Óriásinak tűnik az újrajátszhatósága a sok faj miatt! Előnye még, hogy egyszerű, kb. 5 perc a szabály, maga a játék fél óra, ki- bepakolni is egyszerű, alig van kellék a kártyákon meg a táblán kívül. Viszont nyelvfüggőek a kártyák.
Tetszik az a dilemma, hogy ha gyorsabban akarom növelni a mágia paklit, hogy ezáltal több egységet pakoljak fel a táblára, akkor nagy eséllyel gyorsabban fogyasztom el a húzópaklit. Tehát egyik oldalon a lehetőségek bővülnek, másik oldalon viszont szűkülnek, jól el kell találni az egyensúlyt, vagy gyorsan kinyírni a másikat:)
Nekem nagyon tetszett, akár még emelkedhet is a pontszám!
---
Másodjára hosszabb volt a parti, szinte az utolsó kártyáig kijátszottuk, továbbra is nagyon jó, emeltem a pontszámon. A kieg paklik is jók! (egyelőre csak 2 van). Tetszik hogy egzakt és viszonylag egyszerű a szabály.
---
Annyira tetszik, hogy rövid a szabály, rövid egy parti, változatos és sok taktikai lehetőséget rejt, bármilyen paklipárosítással teljesen más egy parti, és a fránya nyelvfüggőség ellenére is kézenfekvőnek érzem, hogy játszani kell vele... :) Szóval mindez annyira tetszik, hogy ünnepélyesen a kedvencek közé került a játék. 9 pont!
---

RATING: 8
One of the most fun games I've played. This rating is based on 1) Funness  2) Cost/Value ratio  3)  Replayability.  Everything about this game is really cool. I normally buy games based on movies, but this creates its own little theme so well that it doesn't need a movie to go with it. This game reminds me of chess with the exception that each piece has health and attacks/moves differently. (Normally movement is limited to 2 spaces i/e one forward, one right and being able to attack opponent's adjacent cards). Cards with the bow symbol can attack cards up to three spaces away. If you're looking for super deep strategy, you won't find it here. This game is medium strategy with just the right amount of luck.  I find that I'm usually in the mood for non heavy strategy games most of the time anyway.

Initial tentative rating is a 6.5, but it could well go up...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Pro's:

1) Great variety in armies and playstyles. Factions feel quite unique and they tie together very well thematically.
2) Cards are very clear and I personally love the art.
3) Right combination of streamlining and complexity through interaction.
4) It is amazing that a game that is so inherently simple can give of the feel of a complex miniatures table top game. I have played Warhammer for many years and find that while it is of course far removed in many ways. I often find it satisfies that same itch whenever I feel the need for it.

Con's:

1) The difficulty levels of the factions can be quite brutal. Some are much more forgiving than others. Elves or benders are by and large much harder to play well with then say Dwarves or Mountain Vargath.
2) I wish the board had a bit more flair to it. It is very efficient but I wish it had some aesthetics with more obvious nods to say terrain.

Side Note:

Speaking of terrain, maybe this is demented and would take away some of the accessibility of the game but I would love an expansion with some buildings beyond just walls. Maybe some buildings that provide special powers for each of the factions that could add to the positioning element and give the game some RTS elements. Though maybe this is a terrible idea.

RATING: 10
What a game! You can learn or teach this game really easily, but that belies the fantastic depth of strategy you will begin to uncover after a few games.

The use of dice is excellently balanced. The game doesn't hinge too much on luck, but demands that you are constantly thinking and making contingency plans for any unexpected outcomes.

Another excellent piece of balancing is the armies included in this set. Each has a unique play-style but they all seem really well matched. In fact, the more you play and puzzle out the different strategies available, the job the designers and play-testers did balancing this game becomes even more impressive.

I love this game. I would give it 11 if I could!

RATING: 8
Summoner Wars represents a terrific game system. Two different game mechanics and experiences are streamlined - card management and tactical gaming - and improbably integrated. What comes about a result is a remarkably elegant result which is lots of fun to play. What I'm struck by mostly is the value of the game. The rules are ultra-simple and the time investment of a two player game is minimal (30 - 45 minutes) but you are rewarded so much for the minimal investments. The game is deeper than it looks and the different decks play more differently than one would think. The Master Set offers a beautiful board on which to play and so many decks that the replayability of the game is now its greatest value. While not a filler, Summoner Wars is a light game which is absolutely perfect when you have two geeks who may not on a given day have the time or energy for War of the Ring. It's a game that fills this sweet spot as no other does for me.

I really enjoyed my first few plays of Summoner Wars. The Master Set is actually a pretty good deal given the variety that comes with six faction decks. I had my ass handed to me three straight times and still had a lot of fun. For such a seemingly light game there are plenty of tough decisions and a lot of room for look-ahead and analysis. Further play will reveal how deep it goes. I will revisit as I play more. Bonus points for ease of play and (fairly) unambiguous rules, which is uncommon in ccg-inspired games.

UPDATE. Traded after sitting unplayed on the shelf for so long. I liked what the game was doing, and it worked quite well, but it's an awfully big box to have sitting around taking up space. I am knocking .5 off the rating for the box size and dimensions. Shipping that thing was a bitch.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I'm a eurogamer as you can tell from my top rated games (8+). However, this game is my guilty pleasure... I just LOVE it! The tons of different factions that play out radically different is a lot of fun to discover, and the gameplay itself is so elegant! In theory I should like the more advanced Mage Wars more as it has more decisions and less luck, but SW is by far the better game in my opinion. Elegant, interesting, tense, fun!

I usually hate luck, but in this game it doesn't bother me as much, although of course it can suck when you have e.g. three dice, need one hit and then only roll misses... And yes I've had lopsided games where one of the players hit on every single die and the other one didn't, but it's very rare and over the course of the game the hits will most likely even out (although I think it's pretty important to get some hits at the start of the game to remove enemy units and get some magic yourself). There is also the luck of the draw, i.e. if you're so unlucky that all of your champions are at the bottom (or even at the top I would argue). Still, I feel like the luck in this game, both the dice rolls and the card draws, is manageable and on an acceptable level, and it really does feel like the best player usually wins.


COMMENT ABOUT THE FOUR PLAYER GAME:

I’ve played SW a bunch of times (as of 2016 70 times), but almost all of my plays have been with 2 players (which is really how the game should be played). However, I've tried it with 4 as a 2vs2 (I have no desire to ever try it with 3 players again other than the one time I did), and it worked very well! There are few team games out there, so I’m always thrilled when I find a good team game. 1775 is another good teamgame, but I found it too swingy due to the turnorder, so I actually think that, so far, SW is one of my favorite team games if not my favorite! It’s awesome with 2, but with 4 it was very good as well! There are only very few rules changes and I found they integrated well into the base game. With 4, I liked how the board warps around so you can move “off the board” from one side and enter on the other side! This also means that the summoners are more exposed I found. Also, if a summoner dies, you can still assist your remaining teammate and your teammate does get some sort of bonus (magic) when you die so everything is definitely not lost yet! Also, I liked how you can discuss strategy etc. with your teammate during the game. The downside, however, is that the game usually goes on for 1,5-2 hours, and that's a bit too long for my taste.

Overall I highly recommend Summoner Wars - it's by far the best game of its kind out there!

Summoner Wars is an unusual game for me because it's the only game that I played dozens of times on my iPhone before finally playing the "real thing." Now that I finally played it, I can rate this sucker. I'm a Summoner Wars fan. I freakin' love this game.

For whatever reason, this game just strikes a positive chord with me--quick turns, quick games, the tension of hand management, dice chucking combat... I just love the mix. It scratches that ol' Magic the Gathering feeling more than any other game I've played. I think a key reason why is that each deck plays very differently. I really admire how they've achieved such a unique feel with each race yet maintained a balance in gameplay.

I've played all the "original" races on the iPhone, but I finally got a chance to play the swamp orcs against the benders. It's another reminder for me about how impressed I am at the diversity they have created with each deck. Each deck feels very unique, with its own tactics, its own champions, and synergy between various cards.

I want to keep playing this game.

Update: ...and I've done just that. With at least 10+ live plays under my belt, I can easily rate this game a 10. I will always want to play this game and I expect it to be a permanent part of my collection. Great freakin' game.

RATING: 8.5
Rating based on 8 plays, 2 player. 

So far, I am very impressed. The multiple factions, and varied strategies for each faction, allows for incredible variety in gameplay and tactics. Also, it bears mentioning that the game can be taught in under 5 minutes. Yet despite its simplicity, it brings deep tactical and strategic decisions. 

Balance wise, the games have all been tight except for one, where my opponent made a few critical errors, and paid the ultimate price. 

Components are good but not spectacular. Card quality is average, but functional. Artwork is nice but nowhere near MtG quality. 

However, this game has one thing going for it that I must mention: Set up and Tear down. Literally less than a minute to set up, and maybe two to take down. With games lasting 30 minutes to an hour, its easy as can be to get 2 or 3 games with different factions played in an evening. Hell, you could realistically play 5 or 6 games in a 3 hour period, and all of them will be very different. 

This has potential to go to a 9 or more. However, I need to log more plays and play more factions before I make that move. For now, I highly recommend it to anyone who wants a quick, super simple, but devilishly deep game. 

EDIT: Well, I burned out on it. I'm not dropping the rating, because frankly, its a fantastic design, but I'm coming to terms with the fact that tactical combat games just aren't my schtick. However, that does not detract from the truly impressive design of this game. If you like this type of thing, you'll adore this. Traded away to a good home.

RATING: 9
EDIT: After playing this for a while, it doesn't see the table too often (not the right group size, the two player situations I'm in don't lend itself to SW), but it is a really fantastic game and I wish I got to play it more.

I just bought the game this week and opening up it was a treat for myself after giving my thesis presentation. 

I have been listening to the Plaid Hat Podcast through the Dicetower Network as a way to satiate my desire for everything board game while I was busy with school. The podcast is great and entertaining, and I knew I had to give Summoner Wars a try. I purchased the Master Set and downloaded the iOS. 

After a good presentation, I came home, opened the game, and booted up the iOS. I looked at the iOS before, but I couldn't make heads or tails of it. I read through the physical rulebook, looked through the decks (great looking cards), and without any friends to play with at that point jumped into my first game. 

It is great! Simplicity means I can convince all of my friends to get into it. I have a friend who loves MtG and will eat up the deck building. I have another friend who used to play Advance Wars religiously, and I can see him loving to card game meets board concept. The number of factions available is amazing, and when you add in deck building I can see this game becoming an experience I can really dive into, or keep it on the surface when I am busy and enjoy a quick game. 

The gameplay mechanics are simple and fantastic, while being thought provoking and providing meaningful decisions. For me this would normally mean analysis paralysis, but because the play time is short, I feel willing to "just go for it" and see what happens when I play a certain angle. 

The one thing I find interesting, not bad, mechanically is that when you attack a unit they do not defend in any way. It makes for an offensively based game, but being one who really gets into imagining what is going on as live action events, I cannot help but feel a little odd at this. I think the choice must have been on purpose, as most games provide retaliation that raises the stakes and provides some additional thought as well as making the roles of range and cc more interesting. 

Either way, I haven't been so excited about a game in a while, and I am eager to jump into it more. 

Doug4lyfe

RATING: 10
Ever have the itch to pull out those nice painted miniatures and clash with another army on the tabletop, replete with fantasy theme and special powers, but only have an hour?  Not going to happen with minis.  It CAN happen with Summoner Wars, though.  This fantastic card game gives you the same feel of moving your units across the table to vanquish your foes, but with a deck of cards.  You almost have to try it to believe me that it feels like a full minis game.  The artwork could be better, but it does its job evoking the theme and setting the tone.  Tons of replayability in the future with deck-building aspects and new factions.  Another MUST HAVE for anyone who enjoys a tactical fantasy battle.

RATING: 7.75
Only a few plays, but feel like the game has an inelegant design.  A few of the things I feel are awkward: moving and attacking with your entire battlefield on the same turn, discarding cards and using discarded cards as your mana, and also having so many different abilities that you must read and know at once.  The game is very simple, but I find playing with new players is a drag, as they feel overwhelmed by all of the text on every card.  If it's like chess, it's like chess with extremely long turns and a pretty high barrier of entry.  I do think it's well balanced, and think the flavor of each deck is interesting.  I also LOVE the board that comes with the game.  I just feel like the game feels sort of clunky and awkward.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Plus expansions/Alliance

Wonderful 2-player game with many factions released that provide a ton of replay value. Each faction provides their own set of tricks, and even the second summoners within those factions provide neat twists. 

The game offers ways to customize your decks, but I love the fact that players don't have to do this and can simply play with the decks as arranged without any modification.

Since you don't shuffle your discards when the deck runs out and you continue play with what you have left, the game reaches the end game easily. This prevents the game from dragging out too long.

Only quips: The Filth faction tends to be a bit more repulsive in their design for my tastes, but they are insanely fun to play. The game can also produce situations (particularly when pitting two defensive factions against one another) where both players would prefer to wait for the other player to act, leading to awkward stalemate moments.

RATING: 4
Simple 2P fantasy wargame that plays quickly and is super easy to learn. Interesting in that it uses rectangles for movement rather than hexes. Combat resolution is very simple, very much like Risk. Good variation in factions makes this worth keeping, I'll look into picking up expansion content in the future.

Playing this again recently made me realise that every time that I want to play a wargame with dice combat, I always prefer Titan or Cave Evil: Warcults as their combat mechanism is far less frustrating, and hex grid maps provide infinitely more interesting spatial decision making.

RATING: 8
2

Voorbereiding :

De spelers kiezen een factie en nemen het bijhorende deck. Bij het deck zit een overzichtskaart en de startopstelling. Naast je summoner zullen er twee muurkaarten en een aantal monsters liggen. De overige kaarten vormen je trekstapel. Gooi met de dobbelsteen om een startspeler te bepalen.

Speelbeurt:

Een speelbeurt bestaat uit 6 fasen. De startspeler slaat de eerste 3 fases over tijdens zijn eerste beurt. 

1/ Kaarten trekken: 

Vul je hand aan tot 5 kaarten. Als je trekstapel leeg is, kan je geen kaarten meer nemen.  

2/ Monsters uitspelen: 

Betaal de kost op de kaart door kaarten van je magic stapel naar je aflegstapel te leggen. Monsters worden op het bord geplaatst, steeds naast een muurkaart.

3/ Eventkaarten uitspelen: 

Betaal de kost op de kaart door kaarten van je magic stapel naar je aflegstapel te leggen. Een event wordt meteen uitgespeeld en uitgevoerd. Na het effect van het evenement gaat de kaart naar de aflegstapel.

4/ Bewegen:

Verplaats maximaal 3 van jouw eenheden (kaarten) hoogstens twee velden. Enkel orthogonale beweging is toegestaan. Verplaatsing door andere kaarten is niet toegestaan.

5/ Aanvallen:

Je mag met maximum 3 eenheden (kaarten) telkens 1 keer aanvallen. Het maakt niet uit of deze eenheden in de vorige  fase al dan niet hebben bewogen. 

Zwaard symbool: melee aanval. 
Boog symbool: aanval binnen een afstand van 3 velden.

Nadat je hebt aangekondigd welke eenheid je aanvalt en welke eenheid je daarvoor gebruikt, gooi je het aantal dobbelstenen dat staat aangegeven op de kaart.

Een resultaat van 3 of hoger is een hit en een resultaat van 1 of 2 is een miss. Elke hit die je gooit, levert 1 wondtoken op voor de eenheid die wordt aangevallen. Heeft hij evenveel wonden als levenspunten, dan is de eenheid verslagen en komt deze op jouw magic-pile terecht.
Dit voer je voor alle aanvallende eenheden uit.

6/ Magie opbouwen:

Je kan ervoor kiezen om kaarten vanuit je hand af te leggen op je magic stapel. Hierdoor kun je de volgende beurt opnieuw kaarten uitspelen.

Elke eenheid en elke summoner hebben speciale eigenschappen die je mag gebruiken tijdens het spel. Zodra jij de enige speler bent met een summoner, win je het spel.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.25
I like the concept of summoner wars, and some of the execution, but a lot of it just kind of bothers me.  Fantasy battle game: sure.  Lots of different factions: absolutely.  Customizable decks (with the expansions): why not.  Simplified design with easily-understandable special powers: yes please.
But again, there are the problems.  I don't like how ranged combat works at all.  They can only shoot in a straight line (no attacking someone who's caddy-corner to you), they can only shoot 3 spaces, and they can't shoot through friendlies (barring special abilities that say otherwise).  Since there's no counterattacks in melee, and units can move 2 spaces a turn, there seems to be zero advantage.  
Also suffers from the 'wide vs tall' problem many games do (more on that elsewhere), but this is an even more extreme case.  If I have a huge expensive guy and you have a bunch of cheap ones, my bruiser can go around picking them off one at a time while they struggle against him.  Your guys are dead in 1 hit usually, and he fights at full efficiency until his last HP.  Add in one more thing: killed units are used as magic power in this game (one per card, regardless of power).  That huge guy you finally managed to knock off is worth 1 MP to you, while the 4 guys he killed pay for another beast from my deck.  Not only that, but you can only attack with 3 dudes a turn, so there's just no incentive to put a lot of them in play (unless you're playing with a 'swarm' faction which breaks those rules).
I think it may just be [i]too[/i] simplified for my tastes.

RATING: 7
If you're going to buy Summoner Wars, this is definitely a decent place to start as it provides 6 factions and a premium board all at a reasonable cost.  Though I'd currently recommend the Alliances Master Set over this one. Rundown of the factions:

Benders: They only have ranged units but those units can put the opponent out of position or put your own units into position.  They also have multiple ways of taking control of enemy units.  Probably one of the trickier races to play with.

Deep Dwarves: Every one of their units are able to spend magic to do something.  Their events revolve around gaining magic or using these abilities for a free cost.  Even the summoner can put cards from the discard pile into the Magic pile but then you'll be limited in attacking that round.

Mountain Vargath: These units are tough.  I don't think any of their units have just a single hit point.  One weakness however is that I don't think they have any ranged units other than a champion.  Their abilities tend to have to do with being on a certain side of the battlefield and getting into a formation.  The summoner would actually prefer to join his units to give them extra attack power.

Swamp Orcs: These are all about their Vine Walls.  These walls will be a pain when you're trying to move into the Orcs side of the field and also help enhance a lot of the Orcs abilities.  These guys also have one of the strongest common units but it does come at a price as it's quite expensive.

Shadow Elves: A lot of the Shadow Elves abilities revolve around advancing on opponents as does some of their events.  They tend to be fragile but also pack a bit of a punch.

Sand Goblins: They seem to have 2 play styles: turtling or offensive.  Turtling can work because a lot of their units have defensive capabilities.  If they go on the offensive, they are also able to move around opponents units.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Summoner Wars, 2009
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
2
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
[b]Rating based on – 5+ plays, 2 player[/b]
This is a fast paced, action packed tactical combat card game where you combine quick and dirty fighting with spell slinging in order to take out your opponents' Summoner. It feels like a miniatures skirmish game but it's all played with cards. If you've played Hearthstone then this feels fairly similar. Use a deck of cards populated with minions (Commons), elite minions (Champions) and spells as either units or magic points with which you summon those units, all in order to eventually eliminate your opponents' Summoner. These units can also help to defend your own Summoner and any enemy units that you eliminate are added to your magic pile enabling you to summon even more units. Tough decisions whether to use your cards as cheap units now, or for the greater good later to summon an elite fighting machine.

Even though we'd not played this style of game before (Seasons comes the closest), it was easy to learn from the rules provided and once you have the basics down any edge cases are dealt with by the special powers on the cards. I love the ease of setup and the fact that you can play factions directly out of the box especially if you have no experience with deck construction, but once you become more experienced with the game if you so desire (and have a particular favourite faction that you love to play) you also have the option to tweak the decks to your specifications with reinforcement packs and second summoners. It's not collectible so you get a great gameplay experience from the get go without having to chase after expansion content. I like the variety of the factions, and that they all feel very different when you play. I wish the artwork was better/more interesting as it's all kind of plain and drab, but the gameplay more than makes up for it in spades.

On to the negatives... Movement can feel fairly restrictive as everything is laid out in a grid and it can be tough to keep ranged units out of the reach of melee units when they need line of sight to attack. Corners are tricky!  Some of the units don't seem to have a great cost-benefit ratio – they are fairly expensive to summon, but they only have one or two lives and it's even worse when they are melee units which have a high probability of getting killed off if they fail to terminate their target at first strike. Combat is decided by die roll so if you have a lot of rubbish rolls then you will find yourself in a tough spot to get out of as you are both losing units [i]and[/i] falling behind on potential magic gained from those units. Surprsing combinations of cards, sneaky tricks of your chosen faction, and a couple of lucky attack misses can pull you out of a hole though, so it's best not to think the game is done until one of the Summoners is dead. Can have very tense and sometimes surprising endings. Very exciting!

Also own: Phoenix Elves, Tundra Orcs, Jungle Elves and Mercenaries Factions all combined in base game box.

Fantastic 2 player game!
[b]Status: KEEPER[/b]

Whatever the case, the Master Set is a must-buy for any experienced Summoner Wars fan.

RATING: 6.5
Pros
-Involves decision making via hand management (resources are gained by discarding cards)
-Requires and rewards strategy and planning
-Good game balance
-Fairly short game time
-Relatively easy to teach
-Can be played as 2v2 despite being a 1v1 game
-Lots of factions/expansions and customizability

Cons
-Dice rolling combat can be frustrating
-Ranged attacks feel very stiff (can't shoot through own units, can't shoot diagonally)
-Very simplistic combat and units (cards only involve cost, health, attack and 1 special ability)

RATING: 7.5
Magic: the Gathering / PokéMon / Yu-Gi-Oh! like game in which you summon minions with different HP in order to attack your opponent's summoner and defend your own. The difference comes from the territorial tactics, as in Summoner Wars you're also moving your minions over the (small) war zone. By which you have some formation play. And the way of summoning is pretty neat as well, using defeated minions and sacrificed cards to bring reinforcements into play around your walls. But apart from that, it's basically the same thing in a new jacket. Though of good quality.

RATING: 8

RATING: 9
If you're interested in Summoner Wars, this is the best place to start. For less than twice the price of one of the starter sets, you get six faction decks (15 possible matchups!) and a hard-mounted board, plus the necessary dice and wound markers.

If you're new to Summoner Wars, I suggest avoiding the Swamp Orcs and the Deep Dwarves until you learn the flow of the game. Start with any of the other four factions.

My gameplay comments can be found under the general listing for the Summoner Wars family.

RATING: 7
Good 2 player game (can be played with 4 if you have 2 copy of the game).  Each player control a race (there's 6 race to choose from) and the goal of the game is to kill the opponent's summoner.  To summun a creature, you need card in your magic pile.  Your magic pile increase when you discard cards from your hand or when you kill an opponent (or even your own) creature.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Summoner Wars is a great tactical game with a clever hand management aspect to it. It's very streamlined and easy to pick up. 

Every unit you kill goes to the discard, which creates tense moments where sometimes the best thing to do is to kill one of your own units before the opponent gets them.

The races play very differently and seem to be well balanced. I like the way the fantasy tropes are remixed here, and can't wait to try some more.

RATING: 8
As others have suggested, Summoner Wars is akin to Magic: the Gathering, in that you summon monsters to the field of play with mana. However, it has the strategic elements of a Chess game as you position your summons and distribute damage among them. Finally, event cards can be used to turn the tide of a particular skirmish.

Each race possesses play mechanics that not only distinguish it from the other 15 armies, but also seem to match the characteristic feel of that race. Some armies require more finesse, while others require an emboldened attack approach.

The turn structure and preconstructed decks seem to favor balance. With the comparatively cheap model of collection to Magic: the Gathering, it's no wonder why many card game players are flocking to Summoner Wars!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
When Summoner Wars first came out, I liked the game, though the paper map was a real turnoff for me. This master set fixes that complaint. I was never a fan of the expansion packs that simply added to existing factions since, as previously discussed, I don't much like sitting around constructing decks/armies. Fortunately, Summoner Wars plays extremely well right out of the box. 

The basic concept is that each player has an army made up of cards that move around the board. It almost feels like a miniatures game on a hex map, except it’s the cards themselves that move around on card-shaped spaces. Not all cards are units; some of them are spells that can be played for immediate effect. 

One of the really brilliant things about this system is how the deck is used. Not only does it contain your units and spells, it is also a source of currency used to bring them into play. Cards from your hand can be placed into your Magic Pile which is used to pay the summoning costs of your units. Since you refill your hand to 5 at the end of each turn, it's tempting to build a ton of magic. However, your deck is razor thin, and if you do this, a few rounds in you will have a full magic pile and no cards left in your deck to spend it on. The balance this requires of you is difficult to do properly, and in fact there may not be a "right answer" in most situations, so it really requires intuition rather than brain-burning calculation.

The second thing that really amazes me about this system is that the different factions are stunningly well-balanced and yet each requires a totally different style of play. The genius of this game is how it takes a simple system and lets all the complexity and interaction flow from the cards themselves.

If Summoner Wars has one flaw, it is simply that it's really only a 2-player game. There is a 4-player option in the rules and it simply doesn't work very well. A true minis game has a lot more ways to accommodate teams or odd numbers of players, whereas SW is simply limited by its maps and starting setups. They are a necessary evil to achieve the incredible balance of one faction against another, but it does sometimes make me wish a "battle royale" was a more practical option.

RATING: 9.5
Wow, what an awesome game.  The description doesn't sound too appealing, using cards instead of miniatures, but this game really SHINES once you start playing.  It's a mixture of fantasy and war, magic cards with movements.  The rules are simple and setup is a breeze.  You choose a fraction (race) out of the six included in the box.  Each fraction is unique with their own troops and champions.  Each have their own unique special abilities.   There are Goblins, Elves, Dwarfs, Humans, and many more to choose from.  The game is very balance with every race.  There isn't a bad race to  choose but some might be a little more complicated than others.  If you get this, start playing with Vargath and Shadow Elves, as their abilities are more simple to understand.  There are also expansions where you can purchase more fractions for the game, for a total of 16 fractions.  You will easily get numerous plays from just this Master Set, but if you like it, you will easily want to purchase the other fractions because they are all so cool.  
I'm giving this two very big thumbs UP.  Rating it a 9 for now but can easily see this going higher will more plays.  
Go get it !! (if you like fantasy, tactical, mag
ic, dungeon and dragons, world of warcraft type games)
Don't get it (if you don't like direct conflict)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The best way to get into Summoner Wars. So much variety and replayability just in this box alone, although you will probably find yourself quickly purchasing additional armies. Have to say, I hate the collectible, money-sink nature of CCGs and minis games, and I try not to even purchase too many expansion-heavy games. I like mine to be self contained investments. But... SW is the exception. It's worth every dime for the expansions, they add so much additional value.
That said, onto the factions!

Mountain Vargath: the definitive brute force deck, they are fun, but can be a little too straight forward for my tastes.  They are the Roman legion of Summoner Wars, with nearly all abilities based on troop formations.

Sand Goblins: My second favorite faction in the Master Set. They have tough units, use camouflage and trickery, and are highly adaptable in playstyle.

Shadow Elves: hard time figuring these guys out , they specialize in stealth and board positioning. I suspect I would enjoy them with further plays.

Deep Dwarves: one of my least favorite factions. Just can't get behind their playstyle. 

Swamp Orcs: tricky, but highly unique, and very rewarding when played right. The Swampies envelope the field in vine growth, using these to draw power, defense, and range benefits, while also choking the life out of the enemy. I can see these becoming a favorite.

Benders: My absolute all time favorite faction of  any of the 16 armies. These guys specialize in manipulation, subversion, and shutting down the opponent through psychic power.

RATING: 8.5
2013-02-01

Initial Rating: 7.5 (December 2012)

After playing Summoner Wars on the iPad, I liked it so much that I bought everything for the game I could find. It took me years to play Summoner Wars because I (more or less) dislike the art, however I have found this is a great game and I would love to explore it further. 

I like to play Summoner Wars because it has a lot of depth (mostly tactics but also a little strategy) in a very short time frame. When I have to decide which cards to dump onto the magic pile, I feel like I’m playing Race for the Galaxy. Also it is easy to teach, it has a lot of armies and I love the fantastic theme (although it doesn’t have any real background). Its strongest point is the short playtime, I really prefer to play Mage Wars (or, I hope, Dungeon Command) over this, but many times I don’t have the time.

I love the mounted board, I really prefer it over the paper one. But what I REALLY DISLIKE is that I can´t fit my sleeved armies in the box anymore. They fit but it was bending the sleeves so I had to take it out. :angry: I still don’t understand why many publishers doesn’t allow for this when they publish a game. Mage Wars cards fit perfectly in the box and spell books with all the cards sleeved. Also the cards can be scratched (and marked) very easily. 

I’m not really sold on the customization aspect of the game. I still feel that I’m new to the game, but it seems to me, that the game offers little in this regard as you will always choose the best cards in your army and it is fairly obvious what card is better. I will explore this further, but even if this fails, it continues to be a great game for me just as it is with the regular armies. 

I have only played 3 times with the Master Box, so far it appears the Mountain Vargath and Swamp Orcs to be the strongest, but as I said, I have little experience. I will comment when I have played more times. 
Summoner Wars is a light medium game that I always want to play. I really hope my girlfriend likes it when she plays it.

RATING: 10
What an excellent board game! Simple to learn, difficult to master, a game not overly complex that promises varieties. I enjoy it a lot, partially also because i'm a fantasy theme hard core fan. But the game mechanic deserves the credit for making it highly enjoyable and fun. Bought all the expansions immediately after one play. 

[Update 7th Oct 2014] After more than two years of consistent playing it and now having all the expansions to date (with Alliance coming soon), I must say that this is a truly wonderful and excellent game! I have no regret, instead,  full of praise for such an enjoyable game. Thanks to BGG, that's how I came to know about this game. All gamers must give it a try at least once...

[Update 13th January 2017] This is my sixth year of playing this game and I have all the collections of cards, including Alliance, except Second batch of Second Summoners. I will definitely get them later. But what I like to share is simple this: this game is not entirely balanced. not entirely easy to play, not entirely fast to finish, not entirely appealing to all gamers, not entirely cheap to purchase and not entirely beautiful to look at. But it has again and again proven to me, it's one of those rare board games that you just won't get tired of them, in fact, you want more after each game! Lots of varieties, lots of surprises, lots of theme, lots of decisions and options, an awesome game! I will never regret having it and playing it, even though sometimes I loss too.

RATING: 9
Not quite sure why this game works as well as it does.  It's not all that original (different "races", with cards with life-points, strength, and special powers). Yes, it's a card game played on a board, but even there, it's like a million other abstracts.  But, mysteriously, somehow each time I play I end up with an interesting challenge and a down-to-the wire finish. With surprising evocative narrative considering how abstract it all is. And, obviously, I'm not the only one. I like how the powers match the traits of the race: you need to play to their traits or you'll lose.  My sense is that the designer skillfully made it look easy, with lots of tweaking behind the scenes. I'm not a MtG fan, so even more puzzling why I find myself wanting all the factions. (If the depth or fun vanishes, I'll lower my rating. Addendum 4y later, now playing with my 7yo just as good as I remember.)

RATING: 10
Number of players: 2 

Components: (10)
The cards are of good quality. The text is clear and easy to read and the board is beautiful.
  
Rules: (10)
I understood the rules after my first read through. They're laid out in a logical manner and well written. 

Setup: (10)
Each player will have a reference card that displays where their inital troops should go. Finding those troops and their spot on the board is the only real set up.

Area required to play: (10)
The board is huge, but that is pretty much the only area you need to play. There will be dice used, and you will need a small area to hold the wound token, but these things take up very little room.
 
Fun: (10)
This is one one of the most fun games I have ever played.

Theme Integration / Mechanics: (10)
I feel as if every faction plays differently. You have to have a different strategy and apply different tactics depending on the troops that you're using.

Replay Value: (10)
Out of the box I feel like this game has years and years worth of replay value, and with the number of expansions already avaible, I don't see why this game shouldn't be around for decades.

Storage: (10)
Cards.

Accessibility: (10)
This game could be taught in a matter of minutes, even to a non-gamer.

Over-All/Bonuses/Biases: +10
This is a wonderful and original feeling game. The mechanics and the themes used in this game have been used before. They've even been used together. Still, this game plays better than most and I find it to be a very worthwhile addition to my collection.

RATING: 7
- Very very nice playing board, not something I'm used to have with card games

- Card art is sort of bland ... always have to recheck my opponent's cards to remind myself of which card is which unit.  Maybe would've been better if we used minis instead of cards on the actual board.   Maybe it's just that the Master Set races aren't as flashy as I expected ...

- I'm not a huge fan of dice rolls in card games.  However it DOES add some element of strategy because you need to think "Okay, what's gonna happen if I try this and I roll all misses ...".  

So you need to plan for A (Good dice rolls) and B (Bad dice rolls) unlike a card game with no surprises except what's in the hand of your opponent.


All in all I like the mechanics of the game, but I'm not convinced with the Master Set races... I'm happy playing a game now and then and definitely recommend the purchase for somebody who wants variety, but atm it's not a game I'd want to play multiple times per night.   I'll be looking at the previous sets see if it changes my perception of the game ...

RATING: 8.5
A very fun tactical, head-to-head game with great choices that must be made every turn. Can't say enough good things about it. All of the factions are balanced pretty well. If you know what you're doing, you have a good chance of winning with any faction. My only complaint is that it's dice driven without a way to change your luck, once the dice are rolled. You usually hit on a 3+, so the odds favor attacking, which is good. But, it can be brutal to roll over 5 dice on your turn and only land 1 hit...or none. It happened enough to me, that I lost interest in playing it. Otherwise, great game.

RATING: 7
Fun strategy game that combines ccg-style play with boardgame-type tactics. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
I haven't actually played in a few years though our son is now old enough (8 yrs) that we will try it soon.  I rate it a 10 because it is just a perfect game design.  A very simple base set of rules then built upon through the addition of asymmetrical fighting decks.  The only deck building is swapping out a few cards for others in the reinforcement packs.  There is a little randomness in the dice rolling which every once in awhile could swing a game away from you.  Overall though it just stands up so well to repeated playing and is one of the best values in gaming out there.  I also love the use of the tactical maneuvering map which so many of these types of games either eliminate altogether or end up massively overcomplicating how moving around on them works.

RATING: 10
Summoner Wars is one of the best games out there.  The Master Set, though a later addition to the family, is really the best place to start.  In addition to new factions, this set added some much-needed components (i.e. a box to store everything and a nice board).

The advent of the iOS version of the game only heightens my deep love for Summoner Wars.  It is one of the only games my non-gaming family will play, and I feel it has helped me be closer to some family members whom I rarely see.  It is also a great platform for learning the game.

The Master Set, as I mentioned, is another great jumping-on point for new players.  Actually, I would recommend it before the so-called starter sets, just because it has more user-friendly components.  

Short story, Summoner Wars is a masterpiece.  Anyone who doesn't know it yet needs to learn!

RATING: 8
At first I didn't like the game much, probably because of the dice. But since my friend really digs it, after a handful of games I think it's better than what I thought. It's tactically fun and the deck building element, though not necessary, can add a ton of strategy, depend on the match-up. 

For high level play though, this game has a problem: It doesn't have inevitability. Players can actually pass a turn without doing anything and some match-ups can lead to stalemate (when the optimal thing to do in your turn is to pass, since moving or doing anything will hand the advantage to the opponent). There are quite a few debates about this problem on the official forums of the game, though for casual players it shouldn't really be a problem. I doubt the designer will do anything about it. Would have been a 9. 

Also own every card post-Second Summoners.

RATING: N/A
Summoner Wars is a fast-playing, action-packed card game for 2-4 players in which they take on the role of Summoners: powerful beings who harness the power of mysterious Summoning Stones to lead their race to conquest on the war-torn planet of Itharia. These Summoners wield terrible magic on the battlefield, freezing their foes in place, draining their enemies of power, and even bringing rains of fire down from the heavens. But most notoriously, they summon their great race's hordes of warriors to the battlefield, to clash in the never-ending struggle for supremacy. A Summoner is both mage and general, and must combine their wizardly might with clever tactics to defeat the enemy Summoner on the opposite side of the battle.

RATING: 10
Summoner Wars on olnud minu jaoks kõige oluliseim ja põnevaim lauamäng. Hetkel see nii enam ei ole, aga see võib vabalt uuesti muutuda. Võrreldes teiste lauamängudega, olen ma summoner warsi alla kõige rohkem raha matnud. Samuti olen seda ka üsna julgelt üle kahesaja korra mänginud. 100+ mängu iPadi peal, +20 korda arvutis Vassaliga ja arvatavasti nii 100 korda päris elus. 
SW on võtnud male idee ja toonud selle üle 21. sajandisse, lauamängude ajastusse. Selle asemel, et valida, kas sa mängid mustade või valgetega on sul valida 16 factioni vahel ja igas factionis veel 2 summoneri (manaja) vahel. See annab sulle 32 eri võimalust enda leeri valimiseks. Ja kõik factionid on omapärased ja oma mängustiiliga.
Nupud on asendatud kaartidega ja enne iga mängu saad ka oma pakki tuunida (deckbuildida), vastavalt valitud strateegiale. Mäng lõppeb, kui oled vastase summoneri põrmu saatnud.
Siin summoner warsi üle mõtteid mõlgutades, jõudsin arusaamisele, et ta täitis minu jaoks tühimiku, mille oli jätnud yugioh! lahkumine minu elust.

RATING: 10
One of the best games I have ever played. There is enough randomness to keep things unpredictable, but I have never once won or lost a game by chance. All six races are very distinct and each have many levels of strategy to master. 

Note, this is not some teaser product designed to get you to by expansions to fully enjoy the game. There is enough depth in this box to allow for months, possibly years of entertainment. Even if there were no expansions available for this game, I would still be very satisfied with my purchase. 

Every single person I have introduced this game to has verbally said something to the effect of "Wow, that was really fun". This included two complete non-gamers, one of whom told me he usually never had the patience for these types of games.

I strongly recommend getting the Master's Set over the other starter sets available, even if it means waiting a month or so to save up. The Master's Set factions are in my opinion more nuanced than the ones in the other starter sets, and getting six factions adds up to an immense amount to replay value. Also, the full-color board is absolutely gorgeous and easy to move the cards around on. I cannot imagine playing Summoner Wars on some wrinkly grey-scale paper. 

My two extremely minor quibbles are that the cards are about one millimeter longer than standard small cards, making sleeving a pain, and that there aren't enough dice for each player to have their own pool.

I love this game. Just looking at the box makes me happy.      
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
The rules are simple, but all of the different factions add some nice depth to the game.  You may get burned by bad dice rolls once in a while.  However, that can be forgiven since you can have some ridiculously epic matches that play in under an hour.

**Revised thoughts 100+ plays later**
Yes, you will get burned by bad dice rolls.  That's starting to drive me crazy so I dropped my rating from a 10 to a 9.  It's really frustrating to set yourself in a good position offensively and then completely whiff on all of your dice rolls.  Maybe I over-committed and needed to account for the chance of missing all my rolls, but still frustrating no matter what.  Sometimes all my opponent needs is one bad set of attack rolls on my part for them to be able to rally back for the win.  It does keep it interesting...

RATING: 10
Summoner Wars is probably my second most played game of my collection after chess. It is the BEST - by far - implementation of the "Dueling Wizards" concept. Full of theme, extremely balanced factions, unlimited replayability. 
Each faction is radically different with cool and diverse abilities. 

I especially like the limited size of each deck (34 cards) and the hand management aspect of the game. If I had to describe it with only 2 words, these would be "ameritrash chess". 
 
And don't be fooled by the game's entry: this is not a card game, this is a board game with cards.
My favorite factions are "Deep Dwarves" (master set) and "The Filth" (expansion), mainly because these two are the trickiest ones to play with. 

My son's current favorite game.

RATING: 10
I think Summoner Wars in fact uses elements of older cards and miniatures games, but it does it in a pretty original and unique way, the spacial component is great and the armies seem very thematic and well balanced, yet different to play. The artwork, graphic design and materials are all good, but its expandable aspect can make it a little expensive, though. 

Despite luck is present in dice rolls and card drawing I love the feeling of this game, brilliant but simple design all about efficience, good card positioning and luck management, a card you discard to build magic here is a critical choice, every move counts and the player who reads better the match and takes the most out of his event cards, usually will win. Once you get a master set (best place to start) go for some expansions to gain replayability, thanks God it's cheaper than magic. So sad it works well only with 2 players but still an all-time favorite of mine.

I'll track all my Master Set, Alliances and expansions plays at this entry. So far my all-time personal record: 43 Win / 38 Defeats / 1 Unfinished

RATING: 8
I don't LOVE this game, but it's so easy to teach and play, plus it's got so much variety, that I can't help but get all the expansions. It ends up hitting the table more than many games I like better, simply because it's so accessible, teachable and fast. 

This master set is an extremely welcome addition, with the mounted board and the ample storage space. It looks like there's room for 25-30 decks in there! That makes this an essential purchase for anyone who expects to play the game with any regularity.

It really doesn't deserve an 8 rating. However, for being so darn useful and versatile and for being such a convenient way to get maximum utility out of the system (including storage), it gets a bump of one point.

RATING: 7.5
There is a learning curve to this game that makes it a little difficult to introduce to new players.  The replay value is high because it takes a few plays to understand how each faction works, and which faction the opponent chooses also matters.  But this means that each time playing with a new faction is sure to be a bumpy ride.  I wish I had more chances to play with experienced players.

Dec 2013: This game didn't see any plays in the last 6 months because the learning curve is so prohibitive and the master set factions take more advanced understanding of the game to use effectively.  Great game system, but I just don't get it to the table.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
There is a reason why so many people rank this game as an essential must have. It is simple, yet has some real depth. This is one of those games where you really marvel at the designers. No matter which factions each player chooses, this game is so well thought out it is hard to argue one faction will consistently beat another. It is toted as a miniatures game without miniatures, but I would say it is a lot more like chess. Would I say this is a gateway game? Yes, in terms of ease in explaining rules. No in terms of this is a pretty serious game with a lot of depth. If you are trying to get a non gamer friend into games, they could become frustrated that there is a lot of skill in this game and every move has real consequences. If your non gamer friend likes chess, sure start them with this. However if not, then start with something a little lite then move on to this to show how far even a simple game can go.

RATING: 10

A wonderful game for fathers and sons and gamers alike.

RATING: 7.5
Summoner Wars is like the bastard child mash-up of MTG and Chess.  And it makes a lot of sense to me that in order to get the most out of the gaming system -- and it is a system, a wonderful combo attack of modular deck design and strategic play -- you kinda need to devote yourself to the game as much as you'd devote to either MTG or chess.

I play casually, but I can't compete against people who play this game competitively.  At the same time, I can't fault them for enjoying the game; it's a solid design.  It's a well-designed game that rarely hits my table but that I enjoy playing as a dilletante, even when I inevitably lose.  And I guess that speaks volumes.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I'd always assumed Summoner Wars was another entry in the slew of LCG-esque deck builders out there. It wasn't until I picked up a copy of the Master Set on clearance that I realized it was a surprisingly competent tactical miniatures style battle game, only with cards for units instead of little plastic troops. Another surprise was how it's simple rule set has such a high degree of depth as the complexity and variety of play is shuffled off unto the special abilities of the units themselves. 

The end result is a game that's easy to learn to play, but hard to master as each faction, and it's corresponding special abilities, have very different and unique play styles to explore. There are six armies in the box and they run the gamut from tough, melee brawlers to finicky, magic masters. After a few plays with each you'll develop your favorite and really start to nail down some effective tactics with your deck.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A nice 2 player game of attack, attack, attack. Draw units (cards) from your deck, add some units to the board if you have enough "summoning points" (ie kills you've made on previous turns plus cards you've put aside), move 3 units up to 2 spaces each, make attacks with any 3 units within range (some must be adjacent, archers can attack up to 3 spaces away), roll 3's for hits (with modifiers), add wound markers if their life points haven't run out. First to kill the big daddy up the back wins. As you'd expect, you have constant choices on what type of units to summon to the board, from the cheap short-life units to the more expensive, good-luck-killing-this type of unit. There's some event cards in each deck, and each unit has a special type of power, so knowing your deck well will help towards doing well, but there's only 5 or so types of units, plus some event types, so it's not overwhelming to learn. Waiting and generating co-ordinated attacks or defenses to the best advantage of your special powers seems key. The asynchronicity between decks is appealing, as is the quick game play and the constant choices. Lots of luck along the way but that's fine in this presentation and this length.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
At it's most basic, this game is not terribly complicated.  The gameplay is fairly straightforward.  The dice mix things up a bit.  But once you start playing, it gets a bit more serious.  A few turns in, every decision seems to take on more and more weight.  How many commons do I burn as magic?  Which events?  Which heroes?  Who needs to move this turn?

Are there other solid tactical combat games out there?  Sure, but this one is pretty great.  And the master set keeps the options interesting.

RATING: 8
Surprisingly good game. Some of the negative reviews for summoners wars frankly don't know what they are talking about. It's definitely not a boring luck fest. There is luck, but it can be managed and mitigated. 

The game is very balanced and ultimately the better player will win more times than not. 

The game plays quickly and is easy enough for even casual players to grasp. A great balance between gamers game and casual game. Each of the sides have various nuances to master.

This game is a lot of fun for it's weight and play time. Highly recommended.

Note: Of 4 plays I've lost every single time. Not a random luck fest.

edit: Game sold as I needed to make space for other games I was interested in and this one just didn't get played much as other people in my group weren't as interested. I hoped to be able to play the digital version, but it seems to be broken and unsupported. Such a shame.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[b]Comment:[/b] This gives me everything I've ever wanted out of Magic cards but in a non-collectable format. When I was a magic junkie, I used to imagine in my head my army of creatures maneuvering around my opponent's defenses and barriers. Summoner wars comes one step closer to visualizing that thanks to the card grid, where you actually ARE maneuvering around your opponent's defenses. It's almost a miniatures game in terms of it's tactical aspect, but unlike a miniatures game, these cards allow for simple yet complicated abilities that you and your opponent can see right in front of you. As much as I love Heroscape, there are times I don't even worry about the abilities of my opponent's guys just because I'm too impatient to have them read out the card to me from the other end of the table unless it's super relevant to the current combat.

There are cool addon packs that add a minor deckbuilding aspect to the game, which are a great idea, but each time I tinker with the deck I feel like I'm making it less effective than it was out of the box. 

I will say it uses dice for combat, which brings along the sort of randomness that can end your game even if you make every choice correctly. On the whole I don't like using dice in games, but I've learned to allow myself to not be upset when they ruin the best laid plans in these sorts of games.

:star: Art and components
:star: Innovative mechanics
:nostar: Handles 5 or more players
:nostar: Good with min or max players
:star: Low time between turns
:star: Comfortable complexity
:star: Re-playability
:star::star::nostar: Enjoyment

RATING: 7
When Summoner Wars first came out I simply loved it. I partially got my first iphone simply so I could play the then iOS only app. Now I find the game to simply have too many expansions and I also don't have people who like to play anymore. Still is a very good game, but I personally feel much of the strategy has been lost over the years as it becomes increasingly impossible to keep up with all the options that are available, much less predict what your opponent might be planning to do. In the early days it was easy enough to predict what Champion or event your opponent was setting up for and how you could strategically plan for it. Now I find the game to be far too much of simply reacting to your opponent or trying to force the action. I haven't played in a while nor have kept up with anything that came out since Second Summoners and Alliances got released. Will probably be selling/trading all this away sometime as I don't foresee myself returning as the game I once loved is no longer there.  Used to play a ton of this on the app and VASSAL.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A mix of standard LCG battle game and chess. I admire what they've done with these mechanics. Cards as units, simple rules, movement, special abilities. There is a bucketload of cards to explore - 16 factions with deckbuilding options and second summoners, effectively multiplying everything by 2. 

It's not as deep as, say, Android: Netrunner and it's targeted towards younger audience, but it's still a very good game. Factions are varied, with their own theme and playstyle, well balanced. There's a lot of tug of war during the game, and it's your strategy and execution that counts. 

I'm not sure about decbkuilding. There are some options for this, but it's only for units. I guess, you can bump your original deck effectiveness by at most 20%, but you can easily break it and make it unplayable. 

The graphics are, well, mostly generic fantasy. They're passable with some decent exceptions from time to time, but overall they feel a bit bland and childish. Event cards just share the face of the summoner they belong to, which makes them hard to distinguish from others. Also, card layout is very unintuitive - you can get over with it quickly, but it's just bad interface.

Still, a very very very good game.

RATING: 9.79
There are many who bash on this game, but it remains my favorite.  I like that you have to make the best with the card draws you get, because you can burn through the deck faster if you want or need to and you won't have people you play ALWAYS playing every game the same way with the same cards first.  I like the speed of play, the cleverness of the abilities, the tactile movement of the cards, and the randomness from the dice to let you pull off those critical hits at the perfect time to win (or even that tough loss when you really thought you had it in the bag).  I don't know if I necessarily need to keep expanding into second summoners, but everything up to that point is giving me more options than I could hope for in most games.  A great, great game that you do NOT have to play hundreds of times to know what you're doing or be great at (regardless of what a couple of reviewers have said).

Simple (perhaps even simplistic) battle and rules....but the quick play is what makes this appealing.  You don't need to study/know all the cards to have a rewarding game of Summmoner Wars.

RATING: 7.8
This is one of those game that needs some plays to really get the feel of the cards but the game mechanics themselves are quite easy to grasp.  The awesome part of this game is the uniqueness of each faction decks which play completely differently and differently against different factions.  One thing is that you have to get used to the fact that you are going to lose units every round but you will get to summon more and battle on.  There is lucky with the dice roll however, they are skewed heavily to the attacker hence the assumption you will be losing units and sometimes it can be better to take out your own to keep an opponent from get the extra summoning magic.  Really good game that I want to delve more into.  Oh and this really is just a two player game.  i can't imagine playing with more.

RATING: 8
This is one of many games that I own that are essentially 2p only and that I think I would love if I got to play often - but that my wife doesn't, and I don't really do any 2p gaming except with her.

So I won't get enough games to be able to really explore the different factions and choose the ones which I like best - but this has many things which I love in games, all in one box. Hand management, many different and varied decks to learn strategies for, and the chesslike feel of moving things around a board to try to destroy your opponent's pieces. I'm less excited by it now than when I first got it, as there have been so many other games I've got into since then - but I'd still be delighted to play this in the unlikely event that I can ever get a game.

RATING: 9
Jorn ([url=https://boardgamegeek.com/user/Moonhawk]Moonhawk[/url]) bought this game at Essen 2013. Though I took a look at it then, and liked the artwork, I didn't give the game any further thought. It wasn't until I watched the [url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LT4054SBojw&list=PL189336052F027A32]video series[/url] by Watch it Played - in preparation for my first game with Jorn, that I saw how brilliant this game is.

Both players are Summoners - powerful figures from different races, who battle each other with warriors and magic they can call upon with their Summoning Stone. Their goal is to beat the other Summoner into submission. 

Each player has an equal deck of cards, with the same number of different types (Events, Champions, Commons) but different special abilities. Each turn they get to summon new units, use events, move and attack with three different units (not necessarily the ones that moved).

The magic needed to summon units is gathered by either knocking out units (both yours or the opponent's), or placing cards from your own hand into your magic pile at the end of the turn. This is important deck management, as you don't reshuffle your discard pile. Once you're out oof cards to draw, you have to make do with what you've got left.

The game feels more like a miniatures game, though faster and with less setup time. It is very exciting, and because of the different factions, an additional 'easy to learn - hard to master' element is added. Not only the game itself needs to be mastered, but the best strategy for each Summoner is an interesting puzzle to be solved on its own.

[b]Also includes:[/b]
- [thing=129544]Bodgan[/thing]
- [thing=88328]Khan Queso[/thing]
- [thing=92934]Khexhu[/thing]
- [thing=88329]Sairook[/thing]

RATING: 5
I blame myself and not the game. But I think this might be one of my biggest disappointments of 2014 for games that are new to me.

I already know that my wife and I don't really like these card-based fantasy fighting games. They are kind of fiddly and have a lot of text on the cards that breaks the rules. And the direct attacking isn't usually very satisfying to us.

So why did I get this? I guess it was shiny and new and inexpensive. And the high ranking on BGG is always intriguing to me.

But it's just not our kind of game. The cards are kind of low quality, so I guess I blame the game for that. But we just don't really enjoy learning all the different factions and reading the various text on the cards. The game itself seems like it'd be good and well designed; however, it's not for us.

My 3 oldest sons actually might enjoy this. I might try teaching them to see what they think. And my wife and I might even try it a few more times. In general, though, if the game has a lot of theme and is not dry and Euro-y enough for us, there is a low chance we will enjoy it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Games with different draw decks for each player need to have great gameplay and interactions in order to transform the experience from "when am I going to draw that?" (Samurai and every single CCG out there) to "what can I do with what I have?" (Chaos in the Old World). Had my doubts about Summoner Wars because of the simple rules, but I'm happily surprised by the tough decisions, often resulting in immediate feedback. Manoeuvre is the obvious comparison/inspiration, but I really like the dynamism here with wildly asymmetric powers, small board and move-3 attack-3 instead of Manoeuvre's move-1, attack-1 slugfest that takes forever to get going. Also have always loved the theme of magic armies colliding (from my Age of Wonders days), and love how the different decks convey the characteristics of each fantasy race.

I like the model of providing for a balanced "sealed" play that remains interesting because of all the different faction matchups, instead of forcing the LCG model on you (in fact, the deckbuilding aspect here is pretty weak and constrained -- I think I like LCGs that are like that!). I used to strive to create interesting decks to pit against each other in my CCG days. Need some more plays to gauge the balance, but it seems on first glance that the sides are merely different, not more powerful than each other, requiring creativity in each play (as opposed to CCGs, where I knew Deck A would always beat Deck B).

4+4

RATING: 7
Good Game.
To me it has the feel of a simple miniatures war game mixed with a magic feel. Instead of figures you have cards displaying all your information. A person can build a light game strategy but luck will adjust how your real strategy will play out. After playing 4 games the roll of the dice determined the winner. Most likely we played the game with the wrong mind set. We played with too much planning assuming your plan will win instead of adjusting the possibility of bad dice rolls. The card luck is manageable but the dice luck can determine a winner or loser between equal players. If you play the game knowing this then you will enjoy the game.

Akár négyen is játszható (két játékkal), de tipikus kétszemélyes táblán lépegetős fantasy játék. Többfajta fajjal játszhatnak a játékosok, amelyek egységei és eseményei kártyákon szerepelnek. Ezeket a kártyákat megidézve kerülhetnek fel a táblára. A tábla kétszer 6x4-es. Ezeken lépkednek a harcosok, céljuk az ellenfél idéző főhősének megölése. A játék gyors, pörgős, jól kitalált az idézés menete. Érdekes, hogy a hatoldalú kockával történik a támadás, de a 3 fölötti érték találatnak számít, így kevésbé frusztráló a játék, mint egyes ilyen kockás megoldások, ahol sokkal nagyobb célszámok szerepelnek. Nem lehet védeni alapesetben az ütést, így emiatt gyorsan pörögnek az események. A fajok jól kiegyensúlyozottnak tűnnek, meglehetősen különbözők. Nagyon jó kétszemélyes játékot ismertem meg a Summoner Warsban. A fantasy-t és a táblás lépegetős taktikai játékokat szeretőknek nagyon ajánlott.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Plays logged under Summoner Wars: Alliances Master Set cause the box is prettier.

[b]Game in General[/b]: I'm a sucker for asymmetrical 2 player games, and this one is a lot of fun. The factions are truly diverse.

I'm impressed that each match tends to be exciting and feel much, much bigger than what you're really doing -- pushing cards around a table and rolling dice. There's real tactical and strategic depth here that isn't immediately apparent.

The design of the factions is very uneven however. Earlier designed factions are much less interesting and are prone to degenerate game states (who makes the first move??)  and their abilities and such are much more conservative.

Newer factions (Second Summoners onward) are designed much, much better.

[b]Reinforcements:[/b] For me the niche this game fills is that its quick to set up and play and doesn't have much barrier to entry. For that, I'm really glad that the game is designed for an out-of-the-box faction to be fully competitive and playable and balanced, without resorting to deck modification like a LCG or CCG. So I don't like the "customization" this game offers, but it's a shame that some of the cooler units are found in REinforcements and not the base decks.

[b]2v2 Mode:[/b] I like how it actually changes the scope and scale of the game. More units on the board, more interactions, etc. I think 2v2 Summoner Wars is the better game, but the playtime creeps up so far as to compete with heavier games that it wasn't built to compete with, so I'm torn. I think it'd work better with 4 experienced players, as whenever I've tried it it took too long due to newbies.

(4 Design + 5 Enjoyment)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
Summoner Wars is a cross between chess and MtG. It's asymmetric, with lots of variety. Unfortunately, I find the art muddy and unattractive, enough to detract from my enjoyment. Besides, generic fantasy isn't my favourite theme.

More importantly, I don't find the individual units that interesting. I might have half a dozen orcs or something (which I'm not that excited about to begin with) and they all have the same or similar stats, so there's no sense that any of them matter individually. By contrast, I prefer a game like Pixel Tactics, where every card feels uniquely useful and each choice feels meaningful. That's not to say that Summoner Wars is a bad game. It's just that the design is a bit timid for my tastes. Everything blurs together more than I'd like.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
1 play, Origins demo

A fun, light tactical miniatures-type game but without the miniatures. Interesting play, although I suspect all that die rolling might get annoying if I roll poorly!

--- Summary ---
The board is a grid of card-sized rectangles. Each player has a unique faction deck, with a specific summoner, starting creatures (specifically positioned on their side of the board), and deck. On your turn,
1 Draw Cards - up to your hand size (5). Only go through your draw deck once!
2 Summon Units - by spending mana in mana pool, stronger minions costing more mana; they are placed adjacent to the walls on your half of the board.
3 Play Event Cards - by spending mana
4 Move - up to 3 creatures (2 spaces each) orthogonally (but not new ones, which basically have summoning sickness).
5 Attack - up to 3 of your minions (not necessarily the ones moved), adjacent or ranged depending on creature. Combat is a simple die roll: roll a number of d6 based on the attacker type, scoring hits on rolls 3+. Creatures take hits until they reach their maximum (varies); when you kill something, put it face down in your mana pool.
6 Build Magic - place any cards you don't want from your hand into your mana pool.

Play alternates until one Summoner is finally killed.
