RATING: 7
I'm spoiled by Magic: The Gathering.  I was a long time M:TG player and would still be one if not for the cost (both in money and time) to remain competitive.  But the variety of cards, even just in one new set, have spoiled me for games like this.  It is fun for a short period of time but eventually I miss the sheer volume of options a game like M:TG can give you.

Summoner Wars is plenty good in its own right.  There is a large amount of strategy involved and I love the blending of the miniatures-esque mechanic in the movement with a living card game and the amount of customizability available within each of the classes balanced with some of the locked features such as opening board position and units.  The different classes offer a variety of flavor and play style (though not necessarily balance) and for a cheaper entry fee and upkeep over M:TG this is a fine game.  It's just not one that can hold my interest for an extended period of time.

RATING: 7.5
Very good light skirmish game. Units are cards, so expansions are cheap and easy to produce, though some sort of board is required so it's less portable than it could be. Art is OK.

The best thing about the game is that each faction plays very differently -- there's real variety here. The game system is elegant, with real trade-offs around timing and big units vs small ones.

Combat is dice-based and with low numbers of dice (3+ to wound, generally) so the luck-factor is very real and can be wildly swingy. It's short enough that it doesn't matter, but the game is still more of a filler than real meat. I'm a little disappointed that demolishing opponents' walls is so difficult as to be rarely useful: a missed opportunity for an alternate strategic path.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Instantly became a favorite for my son and I.

Love the tactical nature of the game play (moving your units around the board).  Each faction plays so differently and offers a ton of variety in terms of match ups.  I also like how you have to learn to combine the event cards with your units at just the right time.

Normally I don't like random draws and the hand management that is involved in the game but I know that I will (usually) see most of if not all of my cards.

I don't really care for the art work.  The first card I looked at was the Fire Drake for the Phoenix Elves.  It just looks muted and incomplete.  Not a lot of detail.  It's a negative but it is so outweighed by the fun we have playing the game.

The dice can play a large part of who wins and my son has been pretty upset when his biggest attackers roll all misses.  The game plays pretty fast and we can just play again if there is a quick loss.

We have picked up a quite a lot of games over the past two years and my son's top 10 list seems to fluctuate a lot.  This is one of the few games that I know will be on both of our top 5 lists.

We have been wanting to make a playoff battle royale between our favorite factions.  Need to get started on that...

Update:  My son still likes the game, but we ran into a few games where neither of us wanted to move.  And the dice are still a problem sometimes.  Actually, I think the biggest issue is that my son is becoming more interested in video games.

RATING: 7
A fun game with innovative design decisions. It has interesting tactics, strategy and deck building. It doesn't even feel like a card game. More like a light modern war game (ex. battle lore) or a customizable chess game with theme and dice. It also has some very neat mechanics in this game. Very portable and fast setup time, plays fast also. A really good game makes you think about it when you are not playing it. 

As an old magic player I think this game has playing skill but of course a lot less deck building freedom. One negative thing about this game is that you don't have any freedom over spells. I miss some freedom in deck building. I don't know yet how much luck there is in the higher echelons of play. I would also like to see a little more creativity with more spells.

In this game you can just buy on deck and try to master it and then update it a little over time. It also has a good mobile version.

RATING: N/A
Wall of Games Location: A20
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Summoner Wars is my favorite board/card game of all time. It's easy to learn, teach, and play, and there's phenomenal depth there for anyone who wants to become a master. The luck element can be strong at times, but there are plenty of ways to mitigate it, and it ultimately only makes this wonderful game even more thrilling.

I've written about it a few times, and will continue to do so in the future: http://spacebiff.com/tag/summoner-wars/

This set gives you six great factions.

The BENDERS are all about mind control and forcing enemy troops to move, get stunned, switch sides, or even just disappear into thin air. Their own soldiers aren't all that great at straight-up combat, which is fine because their entire goal is to avoid straight-up combat.

The DEEP DWARVES focus on meticulously keeping track of their magic count. Their abilities are all impressive, but many require an extra magic investment. However, they're one of the few factions with an extra economy option, in this case sometimes pulling cards out of their discard pile and into the magic pile, so as long as they manage their troops well, they can keep fighting long after their opponent has run out of magic.

The MOUNTAIN VARGATH are one of the Master Set's more straightforward factions, focusing on sheer might, lots of melee attacks, and crowding the opponent's side of the board. These goat-folk are a very brutal and enjoyable faction, especially when delivering a beat-down to one of the trickier factions.

The SHADOW ELVES are one of those tricky factions, focusing on ambushes and surprise attacks, as well as truly jerky event cards that will leave their enemies seething. Stealing magic is fun!

The SAND GOBLINS are also a bit more tricky, with their focus on strong common units rather than a few champions. Camouflage and scavenging are the order of the day for these tougher, meaner goblins.

And last are the SWAMP ORCS, which have a special mechanic in their many Vine Walls, which they can gradually spread across the board until they're summoning troops onto their opponent's side and blocking all sorts of movement, while their own guys move unhindered.

Seriously, this game is incredible. Each of the factions (6 here, 16 in total) is distinct and fun to play. This is the best two-player card dueler out there.

RATING: 6
I think Plaid Hat did a decent job of designing a one-on-one skirmish game that is affordable but does not lack in variety and thus, replayability. This game is all card driven, but does offer a significant amount of depth between different factions. Although I am not convinced that all factions are well balanced, the variety of factions alone is noteworthy. In a day and age of Kickstarter-driven mania that offers a box-full of minis with absolutely horrendous game play, it is nice to see that Summoner Wars represent the antithesis of companies that focus more on presentation over substance. It is refreshing that one need not fork out hundreds of dollars for a good product. Two thumbs up for Plaid Hat and Colby Dauch.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Summary: The most played game from my collection. I have read through a large spectrum of reviews of this game and I can understand the general concensus that the game is heavily luck based, I disagree with reasons to support my opinion. It is a game of calculated risks and the element of deck building greatly balances the assymetrical start of the game. A great game for its genre. END


Long version: Firstly, I will acknowledge the vast number of comments regarding luck. Yes, unfavorable dice rolls can ruin a game but a single game doesn't represent any meaningful statistics. In the end, strategy weighs more heavily, and I do not believe my opinion is unfounded. The number of plays I have on this game is in the hundreds. I have spectated even more games. My win percentage isn't close to 50%, it is definitely in my favor. I also only play this game with other experienced SW players. With a much larger sample size than the average reviewer, I can safely say that dice rolls account for very little in a match between experienced players. In newbie games, just like in EVERY game, luck seems to be the deciding factor.

This game is best played with serious board gamers. It is easy to pick up and learn, but unless a player is familiar with every card in the game, the element of blind luck increases significantly. The rules are newbie friendly, but the game is deceptively not. It is an absolute bore to play with a newbie, and as such, I cannot give this game a perfect score. 

Those of you who have played DotA, the learning curve is similar. It is easy to play against someone of your own skill level, but mastering the game is dependent on the most seemingly insignificant details.

Seeing as how I regard this game as a serious competetive play type game, I will only post brief remarks about the theming. It is great but once you are absorbed into the game and have passed the point of blaming the dice, the only thought is the strategy. The game is best played as a first to 3 wins, win by 2.

RATING: 7
Summoner Wars hearkens back to days of Magic, only without the collectibility aspect to it, and with a few more constraints in the board and the set up.  It's a crazy-addictive game of battling against other creatures, tempered with the randomness of the die rolls to keep things a little unexpected.  The deck-building aspect is nice, too, since once players get accustomed to the basic factions, they can step up their game by adding some new characters into the mix.  This is a very cool system with a lot of replayability built into it.  I'm impressed.

3 plays: 2 players

RATING: N/A
Summoner Wars is a fast-playing, action-packed card game for 2-4 players in which they take on the role of Summoners: powerful beings who harness the power of mysterious Summoning Stones to lead their race to conquest on the war-torn planet of Itharia. These Summoners wield terrible magic on the battlefield, freezing their foes in place, draining their enemies of power, and even bringing rains of fire down from the heavens. But most notoriously, they summon their great race's hordes of warriors to the battlefield, to clash in the never-ending struggle for supremacy. A Summoner is both mage and general, and must combine their wizardly might with clever tactics to defeat the enemy Summoner on the opposite side of the battle.
\13\\13\
Strategy shapes the composition of each deck of cards and how they are used. Tactics determine the effectiveness of those cards in battle. Call walls of stone to protect you in combat and serve as magic portals for you to summon your warriors. Call your forces forth and send them in a surging wave against your enemy. Cast spells that bolster your forces and cut down those who would oppose you.
\13\\13\
Victory can come only from the death of your opponent's Summoner...

RATING: 9

I love the fact that each faction plays very differently, Summoner Wars has an almost infinite replay value - no two games will ever feel the same. The battles can be super tense and exciting. Just keep in mind that sometimes the random outcome of dice throwing during critical moments can be super frustrating. Still, there's nothing quite like this game so definitely check it out.

RATING: 8
This games about brutal tactics and nothing more.  Like everyone else, I get in the mood for some RPG or fun when I see the box, but when I play, I quickly remember that it's all about tactics.  I think this game could use a WWII reskin that would really benefit it.

This game lacks intensity, fun, and character.  And it is perhaps so well balanced that when two players of equal skill are playing, the game can actually be really boring.  For what it is, I will rank it an 8, but I feel like I am being generous because most of the people I play with would give this game a 7.  

The strategy and tactics are solid and if that's all you're interested in, there's a good amount of game here, but it just didn't grab me like an actually war-theme would have.

RATING: 10
Terrific game. If you ever want to play a tactical game with different characters/races in a pretty short time with short setup-time this is it! Love how you need to chose to use the cards; magic or units? My only negative point is that I dont like that you can kill your own units to get magic - it just doesnt feel right. For me it would have been better if you just discarded the card instead of putting it in your magic pile. This way you still have the tactical options, but it would feel right thematically. It would also make the champions a bit weaker which is a good thing imo.
